And in the second, the Imam said the suspicion remains also because the woman might choose divorce so that the door of acknowledgment and bequest opens, increasing her right, and the spouses might collude on acknowledging the separation and the completion of iddah, and this suspicion is in the increase so we reject it, and there is no suspicion in the amount of inheritance so we affirm it. Consider his statement: 'And thereby what al-Saruji mentioned is repelled.'
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a key issue in the chapter of divorce during terminal illness. The matn states that if a woman is divorced at her own request during her husband's fatal illness, and the iddah passes, then if he acknowledges or bequeaths something to her, she takes the lesser of that and her inheritance. The commentator, Ibn Nujaym, clarifies that the ruling applies to a revocable divorce (one), not irrevocable, because in a revocable divorce she would have no right to inheritance if she consented to the irrevocable. The core discussion is about the persistence of suspicion (tuhma) regarding collusion between the spouses. Abu Hanifa holds that even after iddah, the suspicion remains in the second scenario (mutual agreement in health) because the woman may have chosen divorce to open the door for acknowledgment or bequest. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that after iddah, she is a stranger (ajnabiyya), so no suspicion exists; this is evidenced by the permissibility of her receiving zakat from him, his testimony for her, and her marriage to another. Abu Hanifa replies that such actions are not customary grounds for collusion, so suspicion remains. The passage then discusses the implication for acknowledging a prior divorce: if a husband acknowledges a divorce from an earlier time, and the wife confirms, the iddah is calculated from the time of divorce according to the apparent meaning of al-Hidayah. However, a fatwa from the scholars of Bukhara and Samarkand states that the iddah starts from the time of acknowledgment to avoid collusion. The commentator resolves this by stating that the ruling depends on evaluating the circumstances: if suspicion of collusion is evident, the fatwa on acknowledgment-based iddah applies; otherwise, the time of divorce is used. The passage concludes by noting the seeming contradiction with the earlier point that in the case of divorce at her request, she does not inherit, but some sources (Jami' al-Fusulayn) hold that she does inherit because the husband is considered an initiator since the divorce was not specifically requested in its irrevocable form. This intra-Hanafi dispute shows the nuanced approach to balancing textual evidence and considerations of collusion.

Key Terms
أبانها (abanaha): To make a woman irrevocable (bain) by divorce, here at her request during terminal illness.
التهمة (al-tuhma): Suspicion of collusion between spouses to increase the wife's share through acknowledgment or bequest.
العدة (al-iddah): The waiting period after divorce before a woman can remarry.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment of a right, such as a debt, by the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the woman can still receive zakat from him.

C) Because she cannot marry another husband.
D) Because the divorce was revocable.

Key Takeaway
When a wife is divorced at her request during the husband's terminal illness, suspicion of collusion (tuhma) persists after iddah per Abu Hanifa, resulting in her taking the lesser of the acknowledged/bequeathed amount and her inheritance, unless circumstances disprove collusion.

The Beginning of Iddah When Acknowledging a Prior Divorce
Discussion of when iddah begins upon acknowledgment of prior divorce, with fatwa differentiation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of takhyeer al-hal to determine when iddah begins when a husband acknowledges a prior divorce and the wife confirms.

Core Idea
The start of iddah after a divorce acknowledgment depends on the apparent suspicion of collusion, not a fixed rule.

When a husband acknowledges a prior divorce and the wife confirms, should the iddah begin from the time of the alleged divorce or from the acknowledgment? The Hanafi school does not give a single answer but instructs the mufti to judge the circumstances. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the two positions and the method of takhyeer al-hal (evaluating the case) that determines which opinion governs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State the position of Muhammad al-Shaybani (iddah from time of divorce) and the position of the scholars of Bukhara and Samarkand (iddah from time of acknowledgment). Understand the basis of each.
The difference arises from the suspicion of collusion (tawadu').
2
Understand the concept of takhyeer al-hal
Takhyeer al-hal means judging the case based on apparent circumstances. Here, the mufti must assess whether the spouses were together or separated at the time of the alleged divorce, and whether collusion is likely.
This is a method to determine which opinion to follow.
3
Analyze the al-Sughdi distinction
Imam Abu Ali al-Sughdi distinguished: if the spouses were separated at the time of the alleged divorce, they are believed and iddah starts from that time; if they were together, collusion is apparent and iddah starts from acknowledgment.
This distinction operationalizes takhyeer al-hal.
4
Apply the method to a scenario
Given a hypothetical couple, determine whether suspicion is apparent. If yes, iddah from acknowledgment; if no, iddah from divorce.
The mufti's role is to weigh the evidence.
5
Note the implications for related rulings
Once suspicion is established, not only does iddah start from acknowledgment, but also the wife cannot receive zakat or testimony in her favor.
The same principle affects other areas.

Source Text

He said in al-Nahr: 'And you are an expert that her withdrawal from him in his illness, which is a time of mercy and compassion, is also apparent in her hostility. And bequeathing to her more may be hope for clearing his liability and reminding of previous affection. And it was established in the iddah regarding the statement of the author of al-Hidayah and our scholars meaning the scholars of Bukhara and Samarkand that they give fatwa in divorce that its beginning is from the time of acknowledgment to negate suspicion and collusion. End. Meaning, the acknowledgment of the sick man to her regarding a debt is not valid, nor to marry her sister or four others. And if the violation of this ruling is due to this suspicion, then one should investigate the places of suspicion and the people who are its loci. Hence al-Sa'di distinguished: what Muhammad mentioned about its beginning from the time of divorce is interpreted as when they were separated from the time to which the divorce was attributed, but if they were together, the lie in his speech is apparent, so they are not believed in the attribution. End. And this, as you see, is apparent in judging the case. And if suspicion is established and its beginning is from the time of acknowledgment according to the fatwa, then testimony should not be accepted, nor is it permissible to pay zakat to her.' I say: The upshot is that those who said the fatwa is that iddah is considered from the time of acknowledgment said that due to suspecting the spouses of collusion. As for those who considered it from the time of divorce, they said that where no suspicion appears, as indicated in the correction of Shaykh Qasim where he said regarding iddah in al-Hidayah: 'Our scholars give fatwa in divorce that its beginning is from the time of acknowledgment to negate the suspicion of collusion, meaning the scholars of Bukhara and Samarkand give fatwa that whoever acknowledges a prior divorce and the wife confirms him while both are suspects of collusion, they are not believed in the attribution, and the beginning is from the time of acknowledgment, and there is no maintenance or housing for the wife due to her confirmation.' Imam Abu Ali al-Sughdi said: 'What is mentioned about the beginning of iddah from the time of divorce is interpreted as when they were separated from the time to which they attributed the divorce, but if they were together, the lie in their speech is apparent, so they are not believed in the attribution.' Shaykh Qasim. And by this it becomes apparent that one does not give fatwa that the beginning of iddah is from the time of divorce or from the time of acknowledgment until the case is judged. If the mufti sees the suspicion apparent, he gives fatwa with the second, otherwise with the first. And this is what al-Saruji mentioned about judging the case. And the issue indicates that if a sick woman uses her mahr which is with her husband as khula' and she is not a relative, then one looks at the named amount in the khula' and at one-third of her wealth if she dies after the completion of the iddah, and at the named amount in the khula' and at the amount of her inheritance from him if she dies before the completion of the iddah, so he gets the lesser. Its completion is in al-Bazzaziyya from the chapter of khula'. And he indicated that what she takes from him has a resemblance to debt and a resemblance to inheritance. For the first, if she wants to take it from the actual estate, the heirs are not obligated to that, but they may give her from other wealth considering her claim that what she takes is a debt. For the second, if something of the estate perishes before division, it is upon all, and if she requests to take it in dinars while the estate is goods, she does not have that. And in Fusul al-Imadi: All this is if her iddah has not ended. As for if the iddah...
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion from the previous lesson but focuses on two separate rulings. First, it addresses the question of when the iddah begins when a husband acknowledges a prior divorce and the wife confirms. The commentator clarifies that the fatwa of the scholars of Bukhara and Samarkand is to start the iddah from the time of acknowledgment to negate suspicion of collusion. However, this is not absolute; it depends on evaluating the circumstances (takhyeer al-hal). Imam Abu Ali al-Sughdi distinguished between cases where the spouses were separated at the time of the alleged divorce (then the iddah starts from the time of divorce) and where they were together (then they are not believed, and the iddah starts from acknowledgment). Thus, the mufti must assess whether suspicion is apparent. The second ruling discusses a sick woman who uses her mahr as khula' (divorce by redemption). In such a case, when she dies, the husband receives the lesser of two amounts: the khula' consideration or her inheritance from him (if she dies before iddah ends) or the khula' consideration or one-third of her wealth (if she dies after iddah). The passage also notes the dual nature of what she takes: it is partly like a debt and partly like an inheritance, affecting how it is paid from her estate. Finally, it mentions that these rulings apply only if her iddah has not ended; if it has ended, different rules apply.

Key Terms
تحكيم الحال (takhyeer al-hal): Judging the case based on the apparent circumstances to determine whether suspicion of collusion exists.
المواضعة (al-muwada'a): Collusion or conspiracy between two parties, here between husband and wife to falsely claim a divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the iddah begin if the spouses were living together at the time of the alleged divorce?
A) From the time of the alleged divorce.
B) From the time of acknowledgment.
C) It depends on the husband's intention.
D) The iddah does not begin because the divorce is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The start of iddah upon acknowledgment of a prior divorce is not fixed; the mufti must assess collusion using takhyeer al-hal.

Khula of a Sick Woman: Determining the Husband's Entitlement
Ruling on sick woman's khula with mahr: calculation of husband's entitlement based on timing of death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the husband's entitlement when a sick woman uses her mahr as khula and dies during or after the iddah.

Core Idea
When a sick woman uses her mahr as khula, the husband gets the lesser of the khula amount and either her inheritance or one-third of her wealth, depending on when she dies.

A sick woman may enter into khula (divorce by redemption) using her mahr as the compensation to the husband. If she dies during the iddah or after it, how much does the husband receive? This lesson explains the Hanafi ruling: the husband gets the lesser of the khula amount and either his inheritance share (if she dies before iddah ends) or one-third of her wealth (if she dies after). The amount taken has a dual nature, affecting how it is paid from the estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A sick woman uses her mahr (which is a debt on the husband) as khula compensation. She is not a relative (so inheritance shares are normal).
The mahr is the dower owed by the husband; using it as khula means the wife forgives the debt in exchange for divorce.
2
Determine the two possible amounts
There are two amounts: the named khula compensation (which is the mahr amount) and either the husband's inheritance share from her (if she dies before iddah ends) or one-third of her wealth (if she dies after iddah).
The husband is an heir if the divorce is not final until iddah ends.
3
Apply the rule: husband gets the lesser
The husband takes whichever is less: the khula amount or the other figure (inheritance or one-third).
This is to prevent the husband from benefiting excessively from the khula combined with inheritance.
4
Understand the dual nature of the amount
What the wife takes (the mahr forgiveness) is partly like a debt (since it was owed) and partly like an inheritance (since the husband might get it back). Therefore, he can take it from any of her wealth, not necessarily from the estate, and if estate property perishes, it is shared.
This affects how the heirs pay the husband.
5
Apply to a scenario
Calculate the husband's entitlement given specific numbers for mahr, inheritance share, and wealth.
If the mahr is 100, inheritance share is 60, he gets 60 (lesser).

Collusion and 'Iddah: The Sick Woman's Khula and Inheritance
Explains rulings on collusion, khula, and 'iddah timing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why suspicion of collusion shifts the start of the 'iddah from the time of divorce to the time of confession, and apply the ruling to determine the husband's share in khula from a sick wife.

Core Idea
Suspicion of collusion between spouses shifts the 'iddah start to prevent inheritance manipulation.

When a sick woman initiates khula by her mahr, or when a dying husband confesses a prior divorce, the timing of the 'iddah becomes critical for inheritance and maintenance. Hanafi jurists recognized that spouses might collude to fabricate a past divorce to benefit the wife. This lesson examines how the principle of tuhmah (suspicion) leads to a flexible ruling: the mufti assesses collusion and decides whether the 'iddah begins at divorce or at confession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal problem: collusion (tuhmah)
The passage addresses the concern that spouses might falsely claim a prior divorce to affect inheritance. The first step is to recognize that collusion is a valid legal consideration (tuhmah al-muwada'ah).
This is a unique Hanafi approach; other schools may not consider collusion as a factor.
2
Determine indicators of collusion
The passage states that if there was obvious hostility and the wife left the husband's service during illness, that indicates no collusion. Otherwise, collusion is suspected. The mufti must evaluate the circumstantial evidence.
Examples include bequeathing more than inheritance to the wife, which suggests the hostility is staged.
3
Analyze the ruling on khula from a sick wife
If a sick woman initiates khula by her mahr (not a relative), the husband takes the lesser of the khula compensation and the inheritance she would receive from him, depending on whether she dies before or after the 'iddah. This dual nature (debt vs. inheritance) affects how assets are handled.
The husband's right is limited to the lesser amount to prevent collusion.
4
Examine the dispute on the start of 'iddah
Two opinions exist: (1) 'iddah begins from the time of divorce, (2) 'iddah begins from the time of confession. The mashayikh of Bukhara and Samarkand adopted the second view to negate collusion. Imam Abu 'Ali al-Sughdi added a nuance: if spouses were separated from the claimed time, the 'iddah is from divorce; if together, from confession.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
5
Apply the mufti's discretion
The mufti judges the situation. If collusion is apparent, fatwa is given that 'iddah starts at confession; otherwise, at divorce. The ruling is not absolute but depends on the circumstances.
This aligns with the principle of 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are judged by their intentions).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الخصومة ليست على حقيقتها كما يفعله أهل الحيل للأغراض انتهى. وظهر بما ذكرنا سهو الشمني في شرح النقاية حيث قال: وفي الذخيرة لا بد من تحكيم الحال فإن كان حال خصومة وغضب يقع الطلاق عليها بهذا الإقرار وإن لم يكن كذلك لا يقع .انتهى. فإن صاحب الذخيرة إنما ذكر تحكيم الحال فيما إذا قالت لك امرأة غيري أو تزوجت علي فقال كل امرأة لي طالق فإنه قال قيل الأولى تحكيم الحال إن كان قد جرى بينهما مشاجرة وخصومة تدل فللأول لو أرادت أن تأخذ من عين التركة ليس على الورثة ذلك بل لهم أن يعطوها من مال آخر اعتباراً لزعمها أن ما تأخذه دين، وللثاني لو هلك شيء من التركة قبل القسمة فهو على الكل ولو طلبت أن تأخذه دنانير والتركة عروض ليس لها ذلك. وفي فصول العمادي : وهذا كله إذا كانت عدتها لم تنقض، أما إذا وقت الإقرار على ما عليه الفتوى فينبغي أن لا تقبل الشهادة ولا يجوز دفع الزكاة لها أيضاً . قلت : والحاصل أن الذين قالوا إن الفتوى على أن العدة تعتبر من وقت الإقرار إنما قالوا ذلك لاتهام الزوجين بالمواضعة أما الذين اعتبروها من وقت الطلاق فإنما قالوا ذلك حيث لم تظهر تهمة يدل على ذلك ما في تصحيح الشيخ قاسم حيث قال أما إذا كانا مجتمعين فالكذب في كلامهما ظاهر فلا يصدقان في الإسناد ا هـ. الشيخ قاسم وبه ظهر أنه لا يفتى بأن ابتداء العدة من وقت الطلاق أو من وقت الإقرار حتى يحكم الحال، فإن رأى المفتي التهمة ظاهرة أفتى بالثاني وإلا أفتى بالأول، وهذا ما قاله السروجي من [؟] عدة [؟] محمد من كلام أنه
Between them there was hostility and she left his service during his illness, so that indicates the absence of collusion (muwada'ah), so there is no suspicion (tuhmah). Otherwise, it is not valid due to suspicion. He refuted it in Fath al-Qadir in another way: that the reality of hostility is not apparent, since bequeathing to her more than the inheritance is apparent that that hostility is not genuine, as people who use tricks for purposes do. End. And it became clear from what we mentioned the error of al-Shumni in Sharh al-Niqayah where he said: In al-Dhakhirah, it is necessary to judge the situation. If it is a case of hostility and anger, divorce occurs upon her by this confession; otherwise it does not occur. End. For the author of al-Dhakhirah only mentioned judging the situation in the case where a woman says to you 'other than me' or 'you married over me' and he said 'every woman of mine is divorced'. He said it was said: the first is to judge the situation: if a quarrel and hostility had occurred between them indicating his anger, divorce also occurs upon her; otherwise it does not occur. End. So al-Saruji analogized our issue here to what is in al-Dhakhirah, as he stated in Fath al-Qadir. And it is not hidden from a sensible person the corruption of the statement of whoever said that explicit divorce only occurs in hostility. And the author of al-Dhakhirah did not mention this issue at all, so how can it be attributed to him? And the issue indicates that if a sick woman seeks khula' by her mahr that is owed to her by the husband, and he is not a relative of hers, then consideration is given to the specified amount in the khula' consideration and to one third of her wealth if she dies after the expiration of the 'iddah, and to the specified amount in the khula' consideration and to the amount of inheritance she receives from him if she dies before the expiration of the 'iddah, so he takes the lesser. Its completion is in al-Bazzaziyyah from the chapter of khula'. And he pointed out that what she takes from him has a resemblance to a debt and a resemblance to inheritance. Regarding the first: if she wants to take from the actual estate, the heirs do not have to give it; rather they can give it to her from other wealth, considering her claim that what she takes is a debt. Regarding the second: if something of the estate perishes before division, it is upon everyone. And if she demands to take it as dinars while the estate is commodities, she does not have that. And in Fusul al-'Imadi: All this is if her 'iddah has not expired. As for when the time of confession according to the fatwa, then testimony should not be accepted and it is also not permissible to pay zakat to her. I (the commenter) say: The gist is that those who said that the fatwa is that the 'iddah is considered from the time of confession only said that due to suspicion of collusion between the spouses. As for those who considered it from the time of divorce, they only said that where no suspicion appears. Evidence of that is what is in Tashih al-Shaykh Qasim where he said regarding the 'iddah: It is said in al-Hidayah: Our mashayikh give fatwa in divorce that its beginning is from the time of confession to negate the suspicion of collusion, meaning that the mashayikh of Bukhara and Samarkand give fatwa that if someone confesses to a prior divorce and the wife confirms him, and they are from the contexts of suspicion, they are not believed regarding the attribution, and the beginning is from the time of confession, and there is no maintenance or housing for the wife due to her confirmation. Imam Abu 'Ali al-Sughdi said: What was mentioned that the beginning of the 'iddah is from the time of divorce is to be interpreted as when they were separated from the time to which they attributed the divorce. As for if they were together, the lying in their speech is apparent, so they are not believed regarding the attribution. End. Shaykh Qasim. And by this it appears that no fatwa is given that the beginning of the 'iddah is from the time of divorce or from the time of confession until the situation is judged. If the mufti sees the suspicion apparent, he gives fatwa by the second; otherwise he gives fatwa by the first. And this is what al-Saruji said from [؟] 'iddah [؟] Muhammad from speech that
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Raiq discussing several interrelated rulings within the chapter of the divorce of the sick. It opens by addressing the issue of collusion (tuhmah) between spouses: if there is obvious hostility and the wife left his service during illness, that indicates no collusion, so the divorce is valid. The author refutes al-Shumni's claim that explicit divorce only occurs in hostility, clarifying that the author of al-Dhakhirah only discussed judging the situation in a different context. The passage then moves to the ruling on a sick woman who initiates khula' by her mahr: the husband takes the lesser of the khula' consideration and her inheritance share, depending on whether she dies before or after the 'iddah. This is because what she receives has a dual nature: it resembles a debt (so she is not entitled to specific assets) and an inheritance (so loss before division is shared). The passage concludes with a detailed discussion on from when the 'iddah is calculated: if collusion is suspected, the 'iddah begins from the time of confession; otherwise from the actual divorce. The fatwa depends on the mufti's assessment of the situation. Key authorities cited include Fath al-Qadir, al-Dhakhirah, al-Niqayah, al-Bazzaziyyah, Fusul al-'Imadi, al-Hidayah, and al-Sughdi.

Key Terms
التهمة (al-tuhmah): Suspicion of collusion between spouses to fabricate a prior divorce for financial gain.
المواضعة (al-muwada'ah): The act of collusion or pre-arranged agreement between spouses to deceive.
العدة (al-'iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce before remarrying.
الخلع (al-khula'): A divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation (usually a portion of her mahr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the 'iddah begin for a wife who confirms her husband's prior divorce, if collusion is suspected?
A) Always from the time of the divorce
B) From the time of the confession
C) From the time of the husband's illness
D) From the time of khula

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when collusion is suspected between spouses, the 'iddah begins at the time of confession rather than the alleged divorce, to prevent manipulation of inheritance.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Divorce by a Man in Mortal Danger: Inheritance for the Wife
Ruling on inheritance for a woman divorced by a man exposing himself to death.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a woman inherits from her husband if he divorced her while exposing himself to death and died from that cause, and explain the basis of this ruling and the dispute over the criterion of 'predominant destruction'.

Core Idea
A divorced wife inherits if the husband divorced her while in mortal danger and dies – he is treated like a sick person.

This lesson deals with an exception to the rule that a divorced woman does not inherit. The source passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq and its commentary clarifies that a healthy man who engages in a duel, presents himself for qisas or stoning, and then divorces his wife, she inherits if he dies from that action. The rationale is that his state is predominantly one of death or fear thereof, so he is annexed to the sick. We will unpack the conditions, the proof, and the internal Hanafi debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
From the matn: if a man duels, or presents himself for qisas or stoning, and then divorces his wife (fa abānahā), she inherits if he dies in that manner or is killed. This applies even if he is besieged or in battle lines.
The divorce is valid and she inherits; this is an exception.
2
Understand the analogy to the sick person
The healthy man in mortal danger is annexed to the sick person's ruling. The reasoning is that his state is 'predominantly one of destruction' (ghālibu hālihi al-halāk).
The sick person's divorce is treated specially because of his condition.
3
Analyze the criterion: actual destruction vs. fear of destruction
There is a scholarly dispute: does 'predominant destruction' mean statistical prevalence of death, or the overwhelming fear of death? The commentator prefers the fear-based interpretation, as fear can be present even if death is not statistically probable.
This affects cases like dueling an equal opponent – fear is present even if death is not certain.
4
Note other life-threatening scenarios
The ruling extends to being on a broken ship, in the mouth of a wild animal, etc. The key is the severe danger, not a specific act.
Collusion (tuhmah) is irrelevant here – the danger is objective.
5
Recognize implications for 'iddah and other rulings
The fatwa that 'iddah is from the time of confession (if suspicion exists) applies only to wills, not to maintenance, housing, testimony, or zakat. For those, 'iddah is always from the time of divorce.
No collusion is possible in those matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأوصى لها فلها الأقل منها ومن إرثها ومن بارز رجلاً أو قدم ليقتل بقود أو رجم فإبانها ورثت إن مات في ذلك الوجه أو قتل ولو محصوراً أو في صف القتال لا ولو قوله: (ومن بارز رجلاً أو قدم ليقتل بقود أو رجم فأبانها ورثت أن مات في الوجه أو قتل) بيان لحكم الصحيح الملحق بالمريض هنا وهو من كان غالب حاله الهلاك كما في النقاية وغيرها. والأولى أن يقال من يخاف عليه الهلاك غالباً على أن الغلبة تتعلق بالخوف وإن لم يكن الواقع غلبة الهلاك فإن في المبارزة لا يكون الهلاك غالباً إلا أن يبرز لمن علم أنه ليس من أقرانه بخلاف غلبة خوف الهلاك ودخل تحته من كان راكب السفينة إذا انكسرت وبقي على لوح أو افترسه السبع وبقي في فمه كما ذكره الشارح، وقد يوهم أن الانكسار شرط لكونه فاراً وليس كذلك فقد قال في المبسوط : فإن تلاطمت الأمواج وخيف الغرق معه ينبغي تحكيم الحال. نعم ما ذكره السروجي من شهادة الخصومة بقصد التهمة غير ظاهر ولذا بحث المحقق ابن الهمام في ذلك . ثم لا يخفى أن الإفتاء بكون العدة من وقت الإقرار حيث ظهرت التهمة إنما هو في حق الوصية لكيلا تأخذ أكثر من ميراثها ولا يلزم اعتبارها من وقت الإقرار في حق سائر الأحكام ولذا لم تجب لها نفقة ولا سكنى، وليس ذلك إلا بناء على وجوب العدة من وقت الطلاق فكذا يعتبر وجوبها من وقت الطلاق فيما لا تهمة فيه كالشهادة ودفع الزكاة لما علمت من التصريح سابقاً بأنه لا عادة في المواضعة في هذه الأشياء قوله : بخلاف غلبة خوف الهلاك) أي فإنها تكون في المبارزة لمن هو فوقه أو مثله فلذا كان الأولى أن يقال من يخاف عليه الهلاك غالباً، وكذا أطلق المصنف قوله ومن بارز رجلاً إذ لو كان المعتبر كون الهلاك غالباً لقيده بكونه أقوى منه وما
And he bequeaths to her, so she takes the lesser of it and of her inheritance. And whoever duels a man or presents himself to be killed by qisas or stoning, and he divorces her, she inherits if he dies in that manner or is killed, even if besieged or in the battle line, no, even if... His statement: (And whoever duels a man or presents himself to be killed by qisas or stoning, and he divorces her, she inherits if he dies in that manner or is killed) is an explanation of the ruling of the healthy person who is annexed to the sick here, and he is the one whose predominant state is destruction, as in al-Niqayah and others. It is better to say: one who is feared for him destruction predominantly, because predominance is attached to fear even if the reality is not predominance of destruction, for in dueling, destruction is not predominant unless he duels someone he knows is not his equal; unlike the predominance of fear of destruction. And included under it is the one who was riding a ship when it broke and he remained on a plank, or a wild beast took him and he remained in its mouth, as the commentator mentioned. And it might give the impression that breaking is a condition for him being a fugitive, but it is not. For it was said in al-Mabsut: If waves collide and drowning is feared with him, the situation should be judged. Yes, what al-Saruji mentioned from the testimony of hostility with the intention of suspicion is not apparent, and therefore al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam investigated that. Then it is not hidden that the fatwa that the 'iddah is from the time of confession where suspicion appears is only regarding the will so that she does not take more than her inheritance, and it is not necessary to consider it from the time of confession in other rulings, and therefore she is not entitled to maintenance or housing. And this is only based on the obligation of 'iddah from the time of divorce, so its obligation is considered from the time of divorce in matters where there is no suspicion, like testimony and payment of zakat, because you know from the earlier statement that there is no practice of collusion in these matters. His statement: (Unlike the predominance of fear of destruction) means it occurs in dueling against someone who is above him or his equal, so it was better to say: one who is feared for him destruction predominantly. Similarly, the author (musannif) said generally 'whoever duels a man', for if the consideration was that destruction is predominant, he would have qualified it with being stronger than him, and...
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq, addressing the case of a healthy person who engages in life-threatening actions and then divorces his wife. The matn states: 'Whoever duels a man or presents himself to be killed by qisas or stoning, and he divorces her (fābanahā), she inherits if he dies in that manner or is killed, even if besieged or in the battle line, no...'. The commentator explains that this healthy person is annexed to the sick person's ruling because his predominant state is destruction. However, 'predominant state' is defined not as actual statistical probability but as the overwhelming fear of death. In dueling, destruction is not predominant unless the opponent is clearly superior; otherwise, fear of death is still present. The commentator extends the ruling to other life-threatening situations like being on a broken ship or in a wild beast's mouth. He notes that collusion (tuhmah) is irrelevant here because the situation is objectively dangerous. He also emphasizes that the earlier ruling on 'iddah from time of confession applies only to wills, not to maintenance, housing, testimony, or zakat, where the 'iddah is always from the time of divorce because collusion is not practiced in those matters. The commentator then clarifies that the matn's absolute expression 'whoever duels a man' is not limited by the opponent's strength; if destruction were the criterion, it would be restricted to cases where the opponent is stronger. Sources cited: al-Niqayah, al-Mabsut, and discussions by al-Saruji and Ibn al-Humam.

Key Terms
المبارزة (al-mubārazah): A duel or one-on-one combat, typically to the death, which is considered life-threatening.
القود (al-qawad): Retaliatory killing (qisas) for murder, where the killer is executed.
الرجم (al-rajm): Stoning to death as a punishment for adultery (zina) for married offenders.
غالب حاله الهلاك (ghālib hālihi al-halāk): His predominant state is destruction; the criterion for annexing a healthy person to the sick.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary reason a woman inherits from her husband if he divorces her while in a duel and dies?
A) The duel makes the divorce invalid.
B) The husband is considered like a sick person due to predominant destruction.
C) The wife is considered an heir because she caused the duel.
D) The divorce was pronounced after the duel.

Key Takeaway
A divorced wife inherits if the husband divorced her while in a life-threatening situation and dies from it, because he is treated like a sick person whose actions are given special consideration.

The Core Ruling of Talaq al-Marid (Firar) and Inheritance
Introductory ruling on talaq al-marid and firar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorce by a terminally ill person and explain why the wife inherits despite the divorce.

Core Idea
A divorce executed in fear of imminent death is firar; the wife inherits to prevent deprivation.

When a person is terminally ill or in imminent danger, a divorce may be used as a 'firar' (flight) to deprive the wife of inheritance. Hanafi law counteracts this by allowing the wife to inherit even after a valid divorce, provided the death occurs within the same state of danger. This lesson unpacks the basic rule and the rationale behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling from the text
Read the opening lines of the passage: 'If a sick person bequeaths to his wife, she takes the lesser of the bequest and her inheritance. And if he duels or is brought for execution and divorces her, she inherits if he dies in that state or is killed.' This establishes the core rule.
2
Understand the concept of firar
The divorce is considered a 'firar' (flight) from inheritance. The ruling prevents the husband from using divorce to disinherit his wife while he is in a state of imminent death.
This applies even if the divorce is valid in all other respects.
3
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario of a sick person divorcing his wife and dying shortly after, determine whether the wife inherits based on the rule and the condition that the death occurred within the same state of danger.
Consider the waiting period (idda) nuances mentioned in the text.

منه كما فعل المصنف خلافاً لما مشى عليه في التنوير . نعم ذكر في النهر أن بعضهم قيد به بناء على اعتبار غلبة الهلاك قوله : (وأشار بقوله إن مات الخ) قال في النهر : وفي قوله إن مات في ذلك الوجه أو قتل عليه دون أن يقول بذلك الوجه دلالة أنه لا فرق بين أن يموت بهذا السبب أو سبب آخر ولذا قال في الأصل : مريض صاحب فراش أبان امرأته ثم قتل ورثته وما في البحر من تلاطم الأمواج قيده الأسبيجابي أن يموت من ذلك الموج، أما لو سكن ثم مات لا ترث مما لا حاجة إليه لأنه في هذه يمت في ذلك الوجه بخلاف ما لو قدم للقتل بسبب من الأسباب المتقدمة : ثم خلي سبيله ثم قتل أو مات فإنه مات في ذلك الوجه ا هـ . قلت : وفيه نظر فإنه لو قتل بعدما خلي سبيله لم يمت في ذلك الوجه فإن الوجه المشار إليه هو كونه قدم للقتل وهو حالة غلبة الهلاك وبعدما خلي سبيله زالت تلك فصار بمنزلة ما إذا سكن الزوج ثم مات ولكن ما ذكره في النهر والبحر تبعاً فيه فتح الحالة
Book of Divorce, Chapter on Divorce of the Sick. And if he bequeaths to her, she takes the lesser of the bequest and her inheritance. And one who duels a man or is brought to be killed by retaliation or stoning, and divorces her, she inherits if he dies in that state or is killed, even if he is besieged or in the battle line; but not if her waiting period expires from the time of his acknowledgment; then if he dies, she takes all that he acknowledged for her or bequeathed. End. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: If he says to her in his illness, 'I had married you in health,' or 'I committed intercourse with the mother of my wife,' etc., and she denies, she is divorced and inherits; not if she affirms him. End. And in it: She claims that her sick husband divorced her thrice, he denies and takes an oath, then she affirms him and he dies; she inherits if she affirmed him before his death, not after. End. And in Sharh al-Wiqayah: Know that the particle 'min' in 'the lesser of it and of her inheritance' is not for the comparative degree; rather 'min' is explanatory, and the comparative is used with the lām. The conjunction wāw means 'or' or is for collection by time. End. Then: (And one who duels a man or is brought to be killed by retaliation or stoning, and divorces her, she inherits if he dies in that state or is killed) Explanation of the ruling of a healthy person annexed to the sick here, he whose state is predominantly destruction. It is better to say one of whom destruction is feared predominantly, for predominance relates to fear even if actual destruction is not predominant. For in dueling, destruction is not predominant unless he duels someone he knows is not his equal, unlike fear of destruction. Under it enters one on a ship that sinks and remains on a plank, or a predator that seizes him and remains in its mouth. There is an illusion that the breaking is a condition for being a 'fleeing' but it is not; for in al-Mabsut: if waves clash and drowning is feared, the situation should be judged. What al-Saruji mentioned about testimony of litigation for purpose of accusation is not apparent. Then it is not hidden that giving fatwa that the waiting period is from the time of acknowledgment where accusation appears is only regarding the bequest so that she does not take more than her inheritance; and it is not necessary to consider it from the time of acknowledgment for other rulings. So she has no maintenance or lodging. That is only based on the obligation of waiting period from the time of divorce. Similarly, it is considered from divorce time in matters without accusation. He said: unlike predominance of fear of destruction, which occurs in dueling against a superior. So the author's absolute statement 'one who duels a man' is general; if predominance of destruction were considered, he would have qualified it with being stronger. And it is like the sick. Similarly in al-Bada'i', and al-Isbijabi restricted it to dying from that wave; if it calms then he dies, she does not inherit. End. And a pregnant woman is not considered 'fleeing' except during labor pains. In al-Mujtaba: there is difference in interpretation of labor pains: some say the pain that does not calm until death or birth, others say even if it calms because pain calms sometimes and flares up, the first is more correct. End. And the consumptive, paralyzed, and bedridden: as long as his condition increases, he is predominantly of destruction; otherwise like a healthy person. And this was the fatwa of Burhan al-A'imma and al-Sadr al-Shahid. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn there are opinions: first, if not old, he is like a sick person; if old, like healthy. Second, if recovery is not hoped with treatment, like healthy; otherwise like sick. Third, if it prolonged and became such that death is not feared, like healthy. Fourth, if he did not become bedridden, like healthy; otherwise sick. Fifth, if he increases daily, he is sick; if decreases and increases, if he dies after a year, like healthy; if before, like sick. End. And he indicated by his saying 'if he dies in that state or is killed' that if he divorced after being brought for execution, then released and then killed or died, he is like the sick and she inherits because his fleeing appears by that divorce and his death followed; it does not matter if by other cause. In Fath al-Qadir: In the time of a spreading plague, do all healthy people have the ruling of the sick? The Shafi'is said yes, but I have not seen it from our scholars. End. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: Then one who has the ruling of the sick, if he divorces her and she dies in the waiting period, she inherits whether he died by that cause or another. Hence in al-Asl: a sick person on his bed if he divorces her and then is killed, she inherits. Isa ibn Aban objected: she does not inherit because death-sickness is a cause for death and it did not exist. But we say: his death is connected to his illness as he did not recover; death can have two causes. This implies that it is better not to restrict the dueler to being stronger as the author did, contrary to what is in al-Tanwir. Yes, in al-Nahr some restricted it based on consideration of predominance of destruction. He said: (And he indicated by his saying 'if he dies in that state...') In al-Nahr: In his saying 'if he dies in that state or is killed' without saying 'by that state' indicates no difference between dying by this cause or another. Hence in al-Asl: a sick man on his bed divorced his wife then was killed, she inherits. What is in al-Bahr about the wave, al-Isbijabi restricted to dying from that wave; if it calms then dies, no inheritance. But that is unnecessary because in this case he dies in that state, unlike if he was brought for execution and then released and then killed or died, he dies in that state. End. I say: There is consideration: if he is killed after release, he did not die in that state, because the state referred to is being brought for execution, and after release that state is gone. So it is like if the husband calmed down then died. But what is in al-Nahr and al-Bahr following Fath.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq on 'Talaq al-Marid' (Divorce of the Sick Person). The central issue is whether a divorce executed by a person in a state of imminent death (whether due to illness, dueling, execution, etc.) is considered a 'firar' (flight) from inheritance, thus entitling the wife to inherit despite the divorce. The text begins by discussing the case where a sick person bequeaths to his wife or acknowledges a debt: she takes the lesser of what is bequeathed/acknowledged and her inheritance, to prevent her from taking more than her legal share. Then it addresses various scenarios: a person who duels (mubaraza) or is led to execution, and divorces his wife; if he dies in that state, she inherits. This includes being besieged or in battle. However, if her waiting period expires from the time of the divorce (or acknowledgment) and then he dies, she takes the full amount acknowledged. The commentary clarifies that the particle 'min' in 'al-aqall minhu wa min al-irth' is explanatory, not comparative; the meaning is she gets whichever is less of the two. The text then details who is considered 'mariid' for this ruling: it extends to anyone whose state is predominantly destruction (ghalabat al-halak), such as a person on a sinking ship or attacked by a predator. The criterion is fear of destruction, not actual destruction. The author discusses the case of a pregnant woman in labor, and chronic ailments like consumption (maslul), paralysis (mafluj), and being bedridden (muq'ad). Various opinions are cited on when such a person is considered like a healthy or sick person. The passage also addresses the nuance that if a person is brought for execution and then released, and later dies, the wife may not inherit because the state of fear is gone. The commentary from Fath al-Qadir mentions that during a plague, the Shafi'is treat all healthy people as sick, but the Hanafis do not have this view. Finally, there is a discussion on the case of a sick man who divorces his wife and then is killed by another cause; the wife still inherits because his death is connected to his illness. This is a refutation of Isa ibn Aban's opinion. The overall rule is that any divorce executed in a state of fear of imminent death is considered firar, and the wife inherits if death occurs within that state.

Key Terms
الفرار (al-firar): A divorce executed by a sick or endangered person with the intention of depriving the wife of inheritance.
غالب الهلاك (ghalabat al-halak): A state where destruction or death is the predominant expectation, based on fear and circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A terminally ill patient divorces his wife and dies two months later from a stroke, not from the illness. According to the passage, does the wife inherit?
A) Yes, because the divorce was in a state of imminent death and death occurred before recovery.
B) No, because he died from a cause unrelated to the illness.
C) Yes, but only if he explicitly intended to disinherit her.
D) No, because the waiting period had expired.

Key Takeaway
A divorce executed in a state of imminent death does not deprive the wife of inheritance; she inherits to prevent fiscal flight (firar).

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
Determining the 'Sick' Person: Ghalabat al-Halak and Various Scenarios
Expansion of who is considered like a sick person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify who is considered like a sick person for inheritance purposes using the criterion of ghalabat al-halak.

Core Idea
Not only the terminally ill, but anyone in a state where death is predominantly feared inherits the same ruling.

The ruling on firar extends beyond the obviously sick. The text expands the definition to include anyone in a state where destruction is the predominant expectation (ghalabat al-halak). This lesson explores the various scenarios: dueling, execution, shipwreck, predator attack, pregnancy, chronic illnesses, and how to determine when a person ceases to be in that state.

Guided Path
1
Define ghalabat al-halak
Understand that the criterion is fear of destruction, not actual destruction. The text says 'it is better to say: one of whom destruction is feared predominantly'.
This nuance is important: the ruling applies even if actual destruction is not the majority outcome, as long as the fear is predominant.
2
List the scenarios from the text
The text explicitly mentions: dueling (mubaraza), being brought for execution (qisas or rajm), being besieged, in the battle line, shipwreck (on a plank), predator attack (in its mouth), pregnant woman in labour, and chronic ailments (consumption, paralysis, being bedridden).
For each, consider the condition of 'ghalabat al-halak'.
3
Determine the boundaries
The text discusses when a person is no longer considered in that state: e.g., after release from execution, after the wave calms, when a chronic illness stabilizes or becomes habitual. The ruling also depends on whether the waiting period has expired.
Note the differences of opinion on chronic illness duration.

فكمريض .اهـ. وأشار بقوله إن مات في ذلك الوجه أو قتل» إلى أنه لو طلق بعدما قدم للقتل ثم خلى سبيله أو حبس ثم قتل أو مات فهو كالمريض ترثه لأنه ظهر فراره بذلك الطلاق ثم ترتب موته فلا يبالي بكونه بغيره Isa ibn Aban objected: she does not inherit because death-sickness is a cause for death and it did not exist. But we say: his death is connected to his illness as he did not recover; death can have two causes. This implies that it is better not to restrict the dueler to being stronger as the author did, contrary to what is in al-Tanwir. Yes, in al-Nahr some restricted it based on consideration of predominance of destruction. He said: (And he indicated by his saying 'if he dies in that state...') In al-Nahr: In his saying 'if he dies in that state or is killed' without saying 'by that state' indicates no difference between dying by this cause or another. Hence in al-Asl: a sick man on his bed divorced his wife then was killed, she inherits. What is in al-Bahr about the wave, al-Isbijabi restricted to dying from that wave; if it calms then dies, no inheritance. But that is unnecessary because in this case he dies in that state, unlike if he was brought for execution and then released and then killed or died, he dies in that state. End. I say: There is consideration: if he is killed after release, he did not die in that state, because the state referred to is being brought for execution, and after release that state is gone. So it is like if the husband calmed down then died. But what is in al-Nahr and al-Bahr following Fath.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq on 'Talaq al-Marid' (Divorce of the Sick Person). The central issue is whether a divorce executed by a person in a state of imminent death (whether due to illness, dueling, execution, etc.) is considered a 'firar' (flight) from inheritance, thus entitling the wife to inherit despite the divorce. The text begins by discussing the case where a sick person bequeaths to his wife or acknowledges a debt: she takes the lesser of what is bequeathed/acknowledged and her inheritance, to prevent her from taking more than her legal share. Then it addresses various scenarios: a person who duels (mubaraza) or is led to execution, and divorces his wife; if he dies in that state, she inherits. This includes being besieged or in battle. However, if her waiting period expires from the time of the divorce (or acknowledgment) and then he dies, she takes the full amount acknowledged. The commentary clarifies that the particle 'min' in 'al-aqall minhu wa min al-irth' is explanatory, not comparative; the meaning is she gets whichever is less of the two. The text then details who is considered 'mariid' for this ruling: it extends to anyone whose state is predominantly destruction (ghalabat al-halak), such as a person on a sinking ship or attacked by a predator. The criterion is fear of destruction, not actual destruction. The author discusses the case of a pregnant woman in labor, and chronic ailments like consumption (maslul), paralysis (mafluj), and being bedridden (muq'ad). Various opinions are cited on when such a person is considered like a healthy or sick person. The passage also addresses the nuance that if a person is brought for execution and then released, and later dies, the wife may not inherit because the state of fear is gone. The commentary from Fath al-Qadir mentions that during a plague, the Shafi'is treat all healthy people as sick, but the Hanafis do not have this view. Finally, there is a discussion on the case of a sick man who divorces his wife and then is killed by another cause; the wife still inherits because his death is connected to his illness. This is a refutation of Isa ibn Aban's opinion. The overall rule is that any divorce executed in a state of fear of imminent death is considered firar, and the wife inherits if death occurs within that state.

Key Terms
غالب الهلاك (ghalabat al-halak): A state where destruction or death is the predominant expectation, based on fear and circumstances.
المبارزة (al-mubaraza): A duel or single combat between two individuals, often to the death.
الطلق (al-talaq): In this context, the pain of childbirth (labor).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT considered a person in a state of ghalabat al-halak?
A) A man dueling a stronger opponent.
B) A person on a ship during a storm, fearing drowning.
C) A pregnant woman experiencing normal pregnancy without labour.
D) A consumptive whose condition is increasing daily.

Key Takeaway
The firar ruling applies to anyone in a state of ghalabat al-halak, not just the terminally ill, and the state is determined by fear of destruction, not actual statistical majority.

Talaq — Divorce

Intra-Hanafi and Inter-Madhhab Disputes on Causation and Plague
Dispute analysis regarding causation and plague

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on the plague, and evaluate Isa ibn Aban's objection within the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school maintains that the wife inherits even if death is from a different cause; the Shafi'is treat all during a plague as sick.

Not all scholars agree on the extent of the firar ruling. Two notable disputes: Isa ibn Aban's objection within the Hanafi school, and the Shafi'i position on the plague. This lesson analyzes these differences and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that if a person in a state of ghalabat al-halak divorces his wife and dies before recovery, the wife inherits even if death is from a different cause. The text cites the case of the sick man on his bed who divorces and is then killed.
This is the majority position, as supported by al-Asl.
2
Present the opposing views
Isa ibn Aban objects: she should not inherit because the death-sickness (marad al-mawt) was not the cause of death. The Shafi'is hold that during a plague, all healthy individuals are treated as sick for this ruling.
3
Analyze the proofs
The Hanafi response is that death can have multiple causes, and as long as the divorce was in the state of fear and death occurs without recovery, the connection is sufficient. The Shafi'i position uses a broader analogy, but the Hanafis do not find it supported in their sources.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In a plague situation, Shafi'is consider all divorces by any healthy person as firar, while Hanafis only consider those in actual fear (e.g., symptomatic). This affects inheritance outcomes.

Book of Divorce, Chapter on Divorce of the Sick. And if he bequeaths to her, she takes the lesser of the bequest and her inheritance. And one who duels a man or is brought to be killed by retaliation or stoning, and divorces her, she inherits if he dies in that state or is killed, even if he is besieged or in the battle line; but not if her waiting period expires from the time of his acknowledgment; then if he dies, she takes all that he acknowledged for her or bequeathed. End. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn: If he says to her in his illness, 'I had married you in health,' or 'I committed intercourse with the mother of my wife,' etc., and she denies, she is divorced and inherits; not if she affirms him. End. And in it: She claims that her sick husband divorced her thrice, he denies and takes an oath, then she affirms him and he dies; she inherits if she affirmed him before his death, not after. End. And in Sharh al-Wiqayah: Know that the particle 'min' in 'the lesser of it and of her inheritance' is not for the comparative degree; rather 'min' is explanatory, and the comparative is used with the lām. The conjunction wāw means 'or' or is for collection by time. End. Then: (And one who duels a man or is brought to be killed by retaliation or stoning, and divorces her, she inherits if he dies in that state or is killed) Explanation of the ruling of a healthy person annexed to the sick here, he whose state is predominantly destruction. It is better to say one of whom destruction is feared predominantly, for predominance relates to fear even if actual destruction is not predominant. For in dueling, destruction is not predominant unless he duels someone he knows is not his equal, unlike fear of destruction. Under it enters one on a ship that sinks and remains on a plank, or a predator that seizes him and remains in its mouth. There is an illusion that the breaking is a condition for being a 'fleeing' but it is not; for in al-Mabsut: if waves clash and drowning is feared, the situation should be judged. What al-Saruji mentioned about testimony of litigation for purpose of accusation is not apparent. Then it is not hidden that giving fatwa that the waiting period is from the time of acknowledgment where accusation appears is only regarding the bequest so that she does not take more than her inheritance; and it is not necessary to consider it from the time of acknowledgment for other rulings. So she has no maintenance or lodging. That is only based on the obligation of waiting period from the time of divorce. Similarly, it is considered from divorce time in matters without accusation. He said: unlike predominance of fear of destruction, which occurs in dueling against a superior. So the author's absolute statement 'one who duels a man' is general; if predominance of destruction were considered, he would have qualified it with being stronger. And it is like the sick. Similarly in al-Bada'i', and al-Isbijabi restricted it to dying from that wave; if it calms then he dies, she does not inherit. End. And a pregnant woman is not considered 'fleeing' except during labor pains. In al-Mujtaba: there is difference in interpretation of labor pains: some say the pain that does not calm until death or birth, others say even if it calms because pain calms sometimes and flares up, the first is more correct. End. And the consumptive, paralyzed, and bedridden: as long as his condition increases, he is predominantly of destruction; otherwise like a healthy person. And this was the fatwa of Burhan al-A'imma and al-Sadr al-Shahid. And in Jami' al-Fusulayn there are opinions: first, if not old, he is like a sick person; if old, like healthy. Second, if recovery is not hoped with treatment, like healthy; otherwise like sick. Third, if it prolonged and became such that death is not feared, like healthy. Fourth, if he did not become bedridden, like healthy; otherwise sick. Fifth, if he increases daily, he is sick; if decreases and increases, if he dies after a year, like healthy; if before, like sick. End. And he indicated by his saying 'if he dies in that state or is killed' that if he divorced after being brought for execution, then released and then killed or died, he is like the sick and she inherits because his fleeing appears by that divorce and his death followed; it does not matter if by other cause. In Fath al-Qadir: In the time of a spreading plague, do all healthy people have the ruling of the sick? The Shafi'is said yes, but I have not seen it from our scholars. End. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: Then one who has the ruling of the sick, if he divorces her and she dies in the waiting period, she inherits whether he died by that cause or another. Hence in al-Asl: a sick person on his bed if he divorces her and then is killed, she inherits. Isa ibn Aban objected: she does not inherit because death-sickness is a cause for death and it did not exist. But we say: his death is connected to his illness as he did not recover; death can have two causes. This implies that it is better not to restrict the dueler to being stronger as the author did, contrary to what is in al-Tanwir. Yes, in al-Nahr some restricted it based on consideration of predominance of destruction. He said: (And he indicated by his saying 'if he dies in that state...') In al-Nahr: In his saying 'if he dies in that state or is killed' without saying 'by that state' indicates no difference between dying by this cause or another. Hence in al-Asl: a sick man on his bed divorced his wife then was killed, she inherits. What is in al-Bahr about the wave, al-Isbijabi restricted to dying from that wave; if it calms then dies, no inheritance. But that is unnecessary because in this case he dies in that state, unlike if he was brought for execution and then released and then killed or died, he dies in that state. End. I say: There is consideration: if he is killed after release, he did not die in that state, because the state referred to is being brought for execution, and after release that state is gone. So it is like if the husband calmed down then died. But what is in al-Nahr and al-Bahr following Fath.

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq on 'Talaq al-Marid' (Divorce of the Sick Person). Key Terms
الطاعون (al-ta'un): A plague or epidemic disease.
عيسى بن أبان (Isa ibn Aban): An early Hanafi scholar (d. 221 AH) known for his strict views on causation in firar cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi response to Isa ibn Aban's objection that the wife should not inherit if the husband dies from a different cause?
A) The wife inherits only if the husband dies from the exact same illness.
B) The wife inherits because death can have multiple causes and the divorce was in a state of fear.
C) The wife does not inherit because the divorce is valid and she is no longer a wife.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the wife inherits even if the husband dies from a different cause, and does not extend the firar ruling to all healthy persons during a plague.

Defining Fatal Illness (Marad al-Mawt) for Inheritance Purposes
Explaining criteria for fatal illness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi criteria for determining whether a person is in a fatal illness (marad al-mawt) and apply those criteria to classify different illness scenarios.

Core Idea
A fatal illness in Hanafi law is one that is progressively worsening and overwhelms hope of recovery; if it stabilizes, it loses its special status.

In Hanafi inheritance law, not every illness qualifies as 'marad al-mawt'. Scholars established precise criteria: progression, bed confinement, prognosis, and duration. This lesson explores the definitions and the five views from Jami' al-Fusulayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is defining 'marad al-mawt'. The ruling is that certain conditions trigger inheritance protections for a divorced wife.
The definition determines whether a divorced wife inherits.
2
Locate the criteria from the text
From the passage, list the key factors: (a) illness is progressively worsening, (b) bed confinement, (c) no hope of recovery, (d) if fluctuating, death within a year makes it fatal.
The text mentions consumptive (maslul), paralytic (mafluj), and bedridden (muq'ad).
3
Distinguish the five views in Jami' al-Fusulayn
The passage cites five opinions: (1) chronic vs. acute, (2) hope of recovery, (3) prolonged with no fear of death, (4) bed confinement, (5) fluctuation with a one-year limit.
This shows the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the exact definition.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a specific illness (e.g., stable chronic condition vs. worsening), determine if the person is considered in fatal illness.
Practice with cases: consumptive worsening? Yes. Controlled diabetes? No.

فهو كالمريض. وكذا في البدائع وقيده الاسبيجابي بأن يموت من ذلك الموج، أما لو سكن ثم مات لا ترث انتهى. والحامل لا تكون فارة إلا في حال الطلق وفي المجتبى : واختلف في تفسير الطلق فقيل الوجع الذي لا يسكن حتى تموت أو تلد، وقيل وإن سكن لأن الوجع يسكن تارة ويهيج أخرى والأول أوجه اهـ. والمسلول والمفلوج والمقعد ما دام يزداد ما به فهو غالب الهلاك وإلا فكالصحيح وبه كان يفتي برهان الأئمة والصدر الشهيد، وذكر في جامع الفصولين فيه أقوالا فنقل أولاً أنه إن لم يكن قديماً فهو كمريض لو قديماً فكصحيح، وثانياً لو لم يرج برؤه بتداو فكصحيح وإلا فكمريض، وثالثاً لو طال وصار بحال لا يخاف منه الموت فكصحيح. واختلف في حداً التطاول فقيل سنة وبعضهم اعتبروا العرف فما يعده تطاولاً فتطاول وإلا فلا ورابعاً إن لم يصر صاحب فراش فصحيح وإلا فمريض. وخامساً لو يزداد كل يوم فهو مريض ولو ينتقص مرة ويزداد أخرى فلو مات بعد سنة فكصحيح ولو مات قبل سنة فكمريض .اهـ. وأشار بقوله إن مات في ذلك الوجه أو قتل» إلى أنه لو طلق بعدما قدم للقتل ثم خلى سبيله أو حبس ثم قتل أو مات فهو كالمريض ترثه لأنه ظهر فراره بذلك الطلاق ثم ترتب موته فلا يبالي بكونه بغيره كالمريض إذا طلق ثم قتل. وفي فتح القدير : وأما في حال فشو الطاعون فهل يكون لكل من الأصحاء حكم المرض؟ فقال به الشافعية ولم أره لمشايخنا .اهـ. وفي جامع الفصولين : ثم من له حكم المريض لو طلقها ومات في العدة ترثه مات بهذه الجهة أو بجهة أخرى ولذا قال في الأصل : مريض صاحب الفراش لو أبانها ثم قتل ترثه طعن فيه عيسى بن أبان فقال : لا ترثه إذ مرض الموت ما هو سبب للموت ولم يوجد ولكنا نقول : قد اتصل الموت بمرضه حين لم يصح حتى مات وقد يكون للموت سببان فلا يتبين بهذا أن مرضه لم يكن مرض موته وأن حقها لم يكن ثابتاً في ماله اهـ .
He is like a sick person. Similarly in al-Bada'i', and al-Isbijabi restricted it to dying from that wave; if it calms then dies, she does not inherit. The pregnant woman is not fleeing except during labor. In al-Mujtaba: they differed in interpretation of 'labor'; it was said the pain that does not calm until she dies or gives birth; it was said even if it calms because pain calms sometimes and flares up others; the first is more appropriate. The consumptive, paralytic, and bedridden: as long as his condition worsens, it is overwhelming destruction; otherwise like a healthy person; and that was the fatwa of Burhan al-A'imma and al-Sadr al-Shahid. In Jami' al-Fusulayn, there are sayings: first, if not chronic, he is like a sick person; if chronic, like healthy. Second, if no hope of recovery through treatment, like healthy; otherwise like sick. Third, if prolonged and became such that death is not feared, like healthy. They differed on the limit of prolongation: some said a year; some considered custom; whatever is considered prolongation is prolongation; fourth, if not confined to bed, like healthy; otherwise sick. Fifth, if it increases daily, he is sick; if decreases sometimes and increases others, if dies after a year, like healthy; if before a year, like sick. He indicated by his saying 'if he dies in that way or is killed' that if he divorces after being brought for execution, then released or imprisoned, then killed or dies, he is like a sick person and she inherits because his flight by that divorce appears and his death follows, so it does not matter if it is by something else, like a sick person who divorces then is killed. In Fath al-Qadir: regarding the time of plague spreading, is every healthy person given the ruling of sickness? The Shafi'is said it; I have not seen it from our scholars. In Jami' al-Fusulayn: then whoever has the ruling of a sick person, if he divorces her and dies during the waiting period, she inherits whether he dies by this cause or another. Therefore it was said in al-Asl: a sick person confined to bed who irrevocably divorces his wife then is killed — she inherits. 'Isa b. Aban objected, saying: she does not inherit because fatal illness is a cause of death and it did not exist. But we say: death connected to his illness since he did not recover until he died, and death can have two causes; thus it is not clear that his illness was not his fatal illness and that her right was not established in his wealth.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explaining the rulings on divorce by a person in a fatal illness. It begins by stating that a person in a situation of overwhelming danger (like being on a stormy sea) is treated like a sick person for inheritance purposes, with the condition that death occurs from that cause; if the storm calms and then he dies, she does not inherit. The case of a pregnant woman is discussed: she is not considered 'fleeing' (to deprive inheritance) except during actual labor. Different interpretations of 'labor' are given. The passage then covers chronic illnesses like consumption, paralysis, and being bedridden: the key is whether the condition is progressively worsening (then it is fatal) or stable (then he is like healthy). Multiple opinions from Jami' al-Fusulayn are cited, including distinctions based on chronicity, hope of recovery, duration, and bed confinement. The fifth view introduces a time-based rule: if the condition fluctuates but he dies within a year, it is fatal; after a year, it is not. The text then discusses the case of a man brought for execution: if he divorces after being brought, then is released and later killed or dies, she still inherits because the divorce was intended to deprive her, and death followed from any cause. A reference to Fath al-Qadir mentions the plague, noting that Shafi'is treat everyone during a plague as sick for inheritance, but Hanafis do not. Finally, a dispute with 'Isa b. Aban is recorded: if a bedridden patient divorces irrevocably and is then killed, does she inherit? 'Isa said no because the fatal illness did not directly cause death, but the Hanafi position is that death connected to the illness (he never recovered) and there can be multiple causes; thus she inherits. This shows the Hanafi principle that the intent to deprive inheritance is key.

Key Terms
مرض الموت (marad al-mawt): A fatal illness from which the person is not expected to recover and which generally leads to death.
طلق (talaq): Labor pain; the pain of childbirth that is severe and often fatal.
فارّ (farr): One who divorces to deprive the wife of inheritance; a 'fleer' from inheritance rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fifth view in Jami' al-Fusulayn, when does a fluctuating illness become fatal?
A) If the person dies within one year
B) If the person dies within six months
C) If the illness increases daily
D) If the person is bedridden

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi definition of fatal illness hinges on progression, hope of recovery, and time until death; a stable or chronic condition without progression does not qualify.

Talaq — Divorce

The Principle of Firar: Inheritance After Divorce During Fatal Illness
Explaining inheritance after divorce in fatal illness and the firar dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of firar to determine whether a divorced wife inherits when her husband dies from a cause other than his initial fatal illness.

Core Idea
If a divorce during fatal illness is a 'flight' (firar) from inheritance, the wife inherits even if death results from a different cause.

The Hanafi school uniquely holds that a divorce during a fatal illness does not automatically cut off inheritance. Instead, the law presumes the divorce was an attempt to deprive the wife of her rightful inheritance (firar). Therefore, she inherits if the husband dies from any cause as long as the illness was ongoing at the time of divorce. This lesson examines the dispute with 'Isa b. Aban and the reasoning behind the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school rules that if a person in a fatal illness divorces his wife and then dies from any cause—including execution or accident—while still in that illness, the wife inherits.
This is based on the principle of firar: the divorce is presumed to be an attempt to deprive her of inheritance.
2
Identify the opposing view
'Isa b. Aban (a Hanafi scholar) argued that if death is from a cause other than the illness, the wife does not inherit because the illness did not cause death.
His view is that fatal illness must be the direct cause of death for the rule to apply.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rely on the idea that death is connected to the illness because the person never recovered. They argue that death can have multiple causes, and the illness was the underlying condition.
The key point is that the husband did not recover from his illness before death; thus, death is linked.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
In a scenario where a bedridden patient divorces irrevocably and is then killed by someone else, the wife inherits according to the majority Hanafi view, but not according to 'Isa b. Aban.
This shows the real-world impact of the difference in opinion.

Source Text

Conditional Divorce in Fatal Illness and Inheritance
Expanding the firar doctrine to conditional divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four scenarios of conditional divorce during fatal illness and determine whether the wife inherits, distinguishing between suspension made in health and in illness.

Core Idea
A divorce suspended during fatal illness is firar; the wife inherits despite the divorce.

This lesson expands on the previous one: not only direct divorce during illness, but also conditional divorce (ta'liq) can be considered firar. The key is whether the suspension itself was made in the husband's fatal illness. If so, the wife inherits even if the condition occurs after his death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the timing of the ta'liq
Determine whether the husband suspended the divorce (ta'liq) during his health or during his fatal illness. This is the decisive factor.
If the suspension was made in health, the wife does not inherit, even if the condition occurs in illness.
2
Classify the divorce type
Confirm that the divorce is ba'in (irrevocable). Only ba'in divorce can effect firar because it immediately severs inheritance rights.
Revocable divorce does not cut inheritance completely.
3
Analyze the condition
Consider the nature of the condition: is it an act of a third party, the husband's own act, the wife's act, or a time? The ruling applies broadly.
Even if the act is unavoidable, the husband could have avoided the suspension itself.
4
Apply the firar presumption
If the ta'liq was made in illness, presume the husband intended to deprive the wife of inheritance. Therefore, she inherits if he dies.
This is based on qiyas: direct divorce in illness → firar, so conditional divorce in illness → also firar.
5
Check delegation scenarios
If the husband delegated divorce in health and the agent divorced in illness while the husband could have dismissed him, treat it as if the husband initiated the divorce in illness.
The husband's inaction is effectively a new agency during illness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
علق طلاقها بفعل أجنبي أو بمجيء الوقت والتعليق والشرط في مرضه أو بفعل نفسه وهما في مرضه أو الشرط فقط أو بفعلها ولا بد لها منه وهما في المرض أو الشرط وفي المصباح : برز الشيء بروزاً من باب قعد ظهر وبارز في الحرب مبارزة وبرازاً فهو مبارز اهـ وفيه والسل بالكسر مرض معروف وأسله الله بالألف أمرضه بذلك فسل هو بالبناء للمفعول وهو مسلول من النوادر ولا يكاد صاحبه يبرأ منه. وفي كتب الطب أنه أمراض الشباب لكثرة الدم فيهم وهو قروح تحدث في الرئة .اهـ. وفيه والفالج مرض يحدث في أحد شقي البدن طولاً فيبطل إحساسه وحركته وربما كان في الشقين ويحدث بغتة إلى آخره . حصن من قوله: (ولو) محصوراً أو في صف القتال (لا أي لا لأن التعليق السابق يصير تطليقاً عند الشرط حكماً لا قصداً ولا ظلم إلا عن قصد فلا يرد تصرفه. والمراد من الطلاق في قوله «علق طلاقها البائن لأن حكم الفرار لا يثبت إلا به . وأطلق في فعل الأجنبي فشمل ما إذا كان له منه بد كدخول الدار أو لا كصلاة الظهر. وأما الوجه الثالث وهو ما إذا علقه بفعل نفسه فلوجود قصد الإبطال. أما بالتعليق أو بمباشرة الشرط في المرض. وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان له بد منه أو لا فإنه وإن لم كأنه أنشأ التوكيل في المرض. ودخل في الأول ما إذا لم يمكنه عزله. ودخل في التعليق بفعله ما إذا قال في صحته إن لم آت البصرة فأنت طالق ثلاثاً فلم يأتها حتى مات ورثته وإن ماتت هي وبقي الزوج ورثها لأنها
